          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

2020-10-17 tuexen Improve the handling of cookie life times. The staleness reported in an error cause is in us, not ms. Enforce limits on the life time via sysct; and socket options consistently. Update the description of the sysctl variable to use the right unit. Also do some minor cleanups. This also fixes an interger overflow issue if the peer can modify the cookie. This was reported by Felix Weinrank by fuzz testing the userland stack and in

OK, so it looks like we landed the cherry-pick for 2094 and then the roll to the modern version (which presumably includes all three fixes, and various other security fixes?) Is that right?



<span class="line"><!---->OK, so it looks like we landed the cherry-pick for 2094 and then the roll to the modern version (which presumably includes all three fixes, and various other security fixes?) Is that right?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In which case the decision is between:



<span class="line"><!---->In which case the decision is between:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Plan A) Merge just 2094 to M88.



<span class="line"><!---->Plan A) Merge just 2094 to M88.<!----></span>



<br>





Plan B) Merge the whole roll to M88.



<span class="line"><!---->Plan B) Merge the whole roll to M88.<!----></span>



<br>





Plan C) Revert the roll from master, cherry-pick 2090 and 2091 to master, then cherry-pick 2094, 2090 and 2091 to M88.



<span class="line"><!---->Plan C) Revert the roll from master, cherry-pick 2090 and 2091 to master, then cherry-pick 2094, 2090 and 2091 to M88.<!----></span>



<br>





Plan D) Merge 2094 to M88, and then cherry-pick 2090 and 2091 directly to M88 without those changes going via master (other than as part of the whole roll)



<span class="line"><!---->Plan D) Merge 2094 to M88, and then cherry-pick 2090 and 2091 directly to M88 without those changes going via master (other than as part of the whole roll)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I do not like plan C because it's complicated for you, and I don't like plan D because I never like to put stuff into a stable branch which hasn't previously lived on Canary. On the other hand I am very loathe not to ship fixes for 2090/2091 ASAP.



<span class="line"><!---->I do not like plan C because it's complicated for you, and I don't like plan D because I never like to put stuff into a stable branch which hasn't previously lived on Canary. On the other hand I am very loathe not to ship fixes for 2090/2091 ASAP.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I think we should do Plan A for the initial M88 release (i.e. just put in the fix for 2094) and then take the entire roll for the first M88 security refresh. It's an unusually big thing to put in a security refresh, but at least by then it'll have had two weeks of Canary time. WDYT?



<span class="line"><!---->I think we should do Plan A for the initial M88 release (i.e. just put in the fix for 2094) and then take the entire roll for the first M88 security refresh. It's an unusually big thing to put in a security refresh, but at least by then it'll have had two weeks of Canary time. WDYT?<!----></span>

> 2020-10-17 tuexen Improve the handling of cookie life times. The staleness reported in an error cause is in us, not ms. Enforce limits on the life time via sysct; and socket options consistently. Update the description of the sysctl variable to use the right unit. Also do some minor cleanups. This also fixes an interger overflow issue if the peer can modify the cookie. This was reported by Felix Weinrank by fuzz testing the userland stack and in

Yes. As standard, our policy is to merge high severity bugs back to the current stable branch which is 87. That's why Sheriffbot did that. In practice, we made the final M87 release yesterday, so everything will be headed to 88 from here on (unless something weird changes). M- and Target- are pretty much synonymous as far as I'm aware. Once M87 officially closes down, Sheriffbot will (I think) bump them to M88, though I can't say I pay too much attention to these particular labels - my world centres around Security_Impact and Merge-Request labels.



<span class="line"><!---->Yes. As standard, our policy is to merge high severity bugs back to the current stable branch which is 87. That's why Sheriffbot did that. In practice, we made the final M87 release yesterday, so everything will be headed to 88 from here on (unless something weird changes). M- and Target- are pretty much synonymous as far as I'm aware. Once M87 officially closes down, Sheriffbot will (I think) bump them to M88, though I can't say I pay too much attention to these particular labels - my world centres around Security_Impact and Merge-Request labels.<!----></span>
